## Text Elements
#saprob ^4kQG4nJZ

conditional probability ^XDjYQBAK

P(E|F) ^PbsZI0E7

probability of getting E given F is true ^Eh63rciw

P(E⋂F)/P(F) ^J1vNUHIu

probability of getting F must be >0 ^MuH7Fj9O

probability of getting E ^ F ^5BW8ILkp

why? ^qStWyubp

as F is true, our sample space/universe gets limited to where F is true  ^VEfkqFse

for E to also be true we take the intersection. ∴ we rescale the intersection with the dimension of F's space ^p3CKxJR2

whole sample space ^ONIx3XHO

P(E|F).P(F)=P(E⋂F) ^ee7ss36M

Product rule ^IabO7YA3

replace conditionals to prove ^XpfGMEjc

law of total probability ^f2EneqnA

E ^aTGFseA7

F ^vB86jI2B

for n ^nnHdzGF1

F₁, F₂, ..., Fₙ form a partition of S (i.e. mutually exclusive and union =S) ^WJ23dEFs

V events E, it holds ^Grjed1ZN

prove in ≈ way ^IodX5wGP

Bayes Theorem ^Lv81qVmd

Example ^8IFRtZTN

yellow and red faced cards ^dAxUgzf7
